                <div class="date-outer">
                 <h2 class="date-header">
                  <span>
                   Sunday, November 4, 2012
                  </span>
                 </h2>
                 <div class="date-posts">
                  <div class="post-outer">
                   <div class="post hentry" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
                    <a name="7799204114475296252">
                    </a>
                    <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
                     Owl Granny Square Crochet Pattern
                    </h3>
                    <div class="post-header">
                     <div class="post-header-line-1">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-7799204114475296252" itemprop="articleBody">
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-kWw5qSTMh44/UJaMRTfSguI/AAAAAAAADTk/l5nh_MNoHuY/s1600/OwlGrannySquare1.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                       <img border="0" height="426" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-kWw5qSTMh44/UJaMRTfSguI/AAAAAAAADTk/l5nh_MNoHuY/s640/OwlGrannySquare1.jpg" width="640"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     <br/>
                     I posted this pattern on my friend Kara's crochet blog,
                     <a href="http://www.petalstopicots.com/2012/08/guest-post-repeat-crafter-me-owl-granny.html">
                      Petals to Picots
                     </a>
                     , back in August in honor of her Granny Month. But I thought I would share it with you again and show you how the owl squares are being used!
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     I made them into an owl bunting for my friend Shannon's owl-themed gender reveal party!
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-D0RL3LEAx24/UJaMP79x9NI/AAAAAAAADTU/aQk1awDdu3Q/s1600/OwlBunting.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                       <img border="0" height="266" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-D0RL3LEAx24/UJaMP79x9NI/AAAAAAAADTU/aQk1awDdu3Q/s400/OwlBunting.jpg" width="400"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     <br/>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-oYZHnXdC29Y/UJaMQjx5NQI/AAAAAAAADTc/ofEl-vKw5q8/s1600/OwlBunting2.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                       <img border="0" height="273" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-oYZHnXdC29Y/UJaMQjx5NQI/AAAAAAAADTc/ofEl-vKw5q8/s400/OwlBunting2.jpg" width="400"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     <br/>
                     It was first displayed over the party food table...
                     <br/>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-rTuw5r5aXoM/UJaMSGb4OBI/AAAAAAAADTs/ooaKGY4BhKU/s1600/OwlSquare_GenderReveal.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                       <img border="0" height="266" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-rTuw5r5aXoM/UJaMSGb4OBI/AAAAAAAADTs/ooaKGY4BhKU/s400/OwlSquare_GenderReveal.jpg" width="400"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     <br/>
                     But now it sits over her daughters crib! They are expecting their baby girl in early January 2013 :)
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-FQLXuy6A1RU/USgqjur8M_I/AAAAAAAAE2E/HeL9-Id4TkY/s1600/IMG_5172.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                       <img border="0" height="266" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-FQLXuy6A1RU/USgqjur8M_I/AAAAAAAAE2E/HeL9-Id4TkY/s400/IMG_5172.jpg" width="400"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: x-small;">
                       Photo courtesy of
                       <a href="https://www.facebook.com/ShannonEricksonPhotography">
                        Shannon Erickson Photography
                       </a>
                      </span>
                     </div>
                     <br/>
                     Of course I would love to make an afghan with this square pattern, but I need more time and patience to take on that type of project right now :) If you are interested in making a blanket with these squares and want to alternate between the owl granny square and a basic granny square, you can follow a basic granny square pattern like
                     <a href="http://www.jpfun.com/patterns/free/granny_squares/f101001basicgranny.shtml">
                      THIS ONE
                     </a>
                     and your squares will be the same size.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-bM03Ie6914s/UJaLMLcSCGI/AAAAAAAADSE/OCcp04K_2rs/s1600/OwlGrannySquare.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                       <img border="0" height="330" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-bM03Ie6914s/UJaLMLcSCGI/AAAAAAAADSE/OCcp04K_2rs/s400/OwlGrannySquare.jpg" width="400"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     <br/>
                     <b>
                      Owl Granny Square Pattern
                     </b>
                     <br/>
                     <b>
                      <br/>
                     </b>
                     Materials:
                     <br/>
                     - Vanna's Choice Yarn
                     <br/>
                     - Size G-6 (4.25 mm) Crochet Hook
                     <br/>
                     - Tapestry need
                     <br/>
                     - Small Black buttons for eyes
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     Abbreviations:
                     <br/>
                     SC = Single Crochet
                     <br/>
                     DC = Double Crochet
                     <br/>
                     HDC = Half Double Crochet
                     <br/>
                     TC = Triple Crochet
                     <br/>
                     Click
                     <a href="http://www.petalstopicots.com/2011/11/how-to-crochet-magic-ring.html">
                      here
                     </a>
                     for how to make a Magic Ring.
                     <br/>
                     <div>
                      <br/>
                     </div>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-Qw8Zzj-1kfE/UJaLZSBcHRI/AAAAAAAADTE/-iKjKwHAr-g/s1600/OwlApplique.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                       <img border="0" height="400" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-Qw8Zzj-1kfE/UJaLZSBcHRI/AAAAAAAADTE/-iKjKwHAr-g/s400/OwlApplique.jpg" width="381"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     <div>
                      <br/>
                     </div>
                     Start by making your owl. This pattern would also make a great appliqu!
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     Magic Ring, Chain 1, 8 HDC in magic ring, join to first HDC, chain 1
                     <br/>
                     Round 2: 2 HDC in each around, join to first HDC, change color  (16 HDC)
                     <br/>
                     Round 3: Chain 2, 2 DC in each around, join to first DC, chain 1 (32 DC)
                     <br/>
                     Round 4: HDC, in next stitch: DC - TC - DC, SC in next 5, in next stitch: DC - TC - DC, HDC in next, slip stitch to join.
                     <br/>
                     fasten off, weave in ends.
                     <br/>
                     <div>
                      <br/>
                     </div>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-XNZ0QWajP3w/UJaLQK4plHI/AAAAAAAADS0/EUUoKMwGWY4/s1600/OwlGranny_Loop1.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                       <img border="0" height="400" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-XNZ0QWajP3w/UJaLQK4plHI/AAAAAAAADS0/EUUoKMwGWY4/s400/OwlGranny_Loop1.jpg" width="266"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     <br/>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-3Hvq3L0zmU0/UJaLPfwmsII/AAAAAAAADSs/srZ71HiArkg/s1600/OwlGranny_Loop.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                       <img border="0" height="266" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-3Hvq3L0zmU0/UJaLPfwmsII/AAAAAAAADSs/srZ71HiArkg/s400/OwlGranny_Loop.jpg" width="400"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     <div>
                      <br/>
                      <div>
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      Turn owl over. You are going to be attaching a series of chain 3's where the brown DC's join the pink (see picture). It's best to start to the right of the ear. Be sure to work clockwise (see photo). To start, draw your hook under the bottom of the DC, chain 3. Now skip every other DC. So your pattern should look like this:
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      SC and chain 3, skip one, SC and chain 3, skip one, SC and chain 3, all the way around. In the end you will end up with 8 places where you have connected with SC's and 8 chain 3 spaces. slip stitch to join to the bottom of the first chain 3.
                     </div>
                     <div>
                      <br/>
                     </div>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-0TypwuMqLrk/UJaLN_a6EVI/AAAAAAAADSU/YWAtnhRYXWg/s1600/OwlGranny_BackConnect.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                       <img border="0" height="266" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-0TypwuMqLrk/UJaLN_a6EVI/AAAAAAAADSU/YWAtnhRYXWg/s400/OwlGranny_BackConnect.jpg" width="400"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <br/>
                     </div>
                     Now working inside your chain 3 spaces...
                     <br/>
                     Chain 3 - 2 DC - Chain 1 - 3 DC all in same space, Chain 1, 3 DC in next space, Chain 1, *3 DC - Chain 1 - 3 DC all in same space, Chain 1, 3 DC in next space, Chain 1, *Around, slip stitch to join to the top of the first chain 3, fasten off.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     With new color and starting in corner space...
                     <br/>
                     Chain 3 - 2 DC - Chain 1 - 3 DC all in same space, Chain 1, 3 DC in next space, Chain 1, 3 DC in next space, *3 DC - Chain 1 - 3 DC all in same space, Chain 1, 3 DC in next space, Chain 1, 3 DC in next space, *around, slip stitch to join to the top of the first chain 3, fasten off.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     With new color and starting in corner space...
                     <br/>
                     Chain 3 - 2 DC - Chain 1 - 3 DC all in same space, Chain 1, 3 DC in next space, Chain 1, 3 DC in next space, Chain 1, 3 DC in next space,* 3 DC in next space - Chain 1 - 3 DC all in same space, Chain 1, 3 DC in next space, Chain 1, 3 DC in next space, Chain 1, 3 DC in next space, *Around, slip stitch to join to the top of the first chain 3, fasten off, weave in all ends.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     This is what the backside of your granny square should look like:
                     <br/>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-NC5g80DHtds/UJaLQh6dGDI/AAAAAAAADS8/FrlFip4ds9c/s1600/OwlGranny_backside.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                       <img border="0" height="266" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-NC5g80DHtds/UJaLQh6dGDI/AAAAAAAADS8/FrlFip4ds9c/s400/OwlGranny_backside.jpg" width="400"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     <div>
                      <br/>
                     </div>
                     Now you can add the embellishments to the owl.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <b>
                      Eyes:
                     </b>
                     <br/>
                     Magic Ring, Chain 1, 8HDC in magic ring, join to first HDC, fasten off leaving a long tail to sew on.
                     <br/>
                     Sew on no larger than 1/2" black buttons in the middle for eyes.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <b>
                      Beak and Feet:
                     </b>
                     <br/>
                     Sew on yellow yarn with tapestry needle. Loop the yarn through 3 times to make both the feet and beak.
                     <br/>
                     <div>
                      <br/>
                     </div>
                     <div>
                      You can download a PDF of this pattern
                      <a href="http://www.scribd.com/doc/112082240/Owl-Granny-Square-Crochet-Pattern">
                       HERE
                      </a>
                      .
                     </div>
                     <div>
                      _______________________________
                     </div>
                     <div>
                      <br/>
                     </div>

      var cursor = null;
      if (items &amp;&amp; items.length &gt; 0) {
        cursor = parseInt(items[items.length - 1].timestamp) + 1;
      }

      var bodyFromEntry = function(entry) {
        if (entry.gd$extendedProperty) {
          for (var k in entry.gd$extendedProperty) {
            if (entry.gd$extendedProperty[k].name == 'blogger.contentRemoved') {
              return '&lt;span class="deleted-comment"&gt;' + entry.content.$t + '&lt;/span&gt;';
            }
          }
        }
        return entry.content.$t;
      }

      var parse = function(data) {
        cursor = null;
        var comments = [];
        if (data &amp;&amp; data.feed &amp;&amp; data.feed.entry) {
          for (var i = 0, entry; entry = data.feed.entry[i]; i++) {
            var comment = {};
            // comment ID, parsed out of the original id format
            var id = /blog-(\d+).post-(\d+)/.exec(entry.id.$t);
            comment.id = id ? id[2] : null;
            comment.body = bodyFromEntry(entry);
            comment.timestamp = Date.parse(entry.published.$t) + '';
            if (entry.author &amp;&amp; entry.author.constructor === Array) {
              var auth = entry.author[0];
              if (auth) {
                comment.author = {
                  name: (auth.name ? auth.name.$t : undefined),
                  profileUrl: (auth.uri ? auth.uri.$t : undefined),
                  avatarUrl: (auth.gd$image ? auth.gd$image.src : undefined)
                };
              }
            }
            if (entry.link) {
              if (entry.link[2]) {
                comment.link = comment.permalink = entry.link[2].href;
              }
              if (entry.link[3]) {
                var pid = /.*comments\/default\/(\d+)\?.*/.exec(entry.link[3].href);
                if (pid &amp;&amp; pid[1]) {
                  comment.parentId = pid[1];
                }
              }
            }
            comment.deleteclass = 'item-control blog-admin';
            if (entry.gd$extendedProperty) {
              for (var k in entry.gd$extendedProperty) {
                if (entry.gd$extendedProperty[k].name == 'blogger.itemClass') {
                  comment.deleteclass += ' ' + entry.gd$extendedProperty[k].value;
                } else if (entry.gd$extendedProperty[k].name == 'blogger.displayTime') {
                  comment.displayTime = entry.gd$extendedProperty[k].value;
                }
              }
            }
            comments.push(comment);
          }
        }
        return comments;
      };

      var paginator = function(callback) {
        if (hasMore()) {
          var url = config.feed + '?alt=json&amp;v=2&amp;orderby=published&amp;reverse=false&amp;max-results=50';
          if (cursor) {
            url += '&amp;published-min=' + new Date(cursor).toISOString();
          }
          window.bloggercomments = function(data) {
            var parsed = parse(data);
            cursor = parsed.length &lt; 50 ? null
                : parseInt(parsed[parsed.length - 1].timestamp) + 1
            callback(parsed);
            window.bloggercomments = null;
          }
          url += '&amp;callback=bloggercomments';
          var script = document.createElement('script');
          script.type = 'text/javascript';
          script.src = url;
          document.getElementsByTagName('head')[0].appendChild(script);
        }
      };
      var hasMore = function() {
        return !!cursor;
      };
      var getMeta = function(key, comment) {
        if ('iswriter' == key) {
          var matches = !!comment.author
              &amp;&amp; comment.author.name == config.authorName
              &amp;&amp; comment.author.profileUrl == config.authorUrl;
          return matches ? 'true' : '';
        } else if ('deletelink' == key) {
          return config.baseUri + '/delete-comment.g?blogID='
               + config.blogId + '&amp;postID=' + comment.id;
        } else if ('deleteclass' == key) {
          return comment.deleteclass;
        }
        return '';
      };

      var replybox = null;
      var replyUrlParts = null;
      var replyParent = undefined;

      var onReply = function(commentId, domId) {
        if (replybox == null) {
          // lazily cache replybox, and adjust to suit this style:
          replybox = document.getElementById('comment-editor');
          if (replybox != null) {
            replybox.height = '250px';
            replybox.style.display = 'block';
            replyUrlParts = replybox.src.split('#');
          }
        }
        if (replybox &amp;&amp; (commentId !== replyParent)) {
          document.getElementById(domId).insertBefore(replybox, null);
          replybox.src = replyUrlParts[0]
              + (commentId ? '&amp;parentID=' + commentId : '')
              + '#' + replyUrlParts[1];
          replyParent = commentId;
        }
      };

      var hash = (window.location.hash || '#').substring(1);
      var startThread, targetComment;
      if (/^comment-form_/.test(hash)) {
        startThread = hash.substring('comment-form_'.length);
      } else if (/^c[0-9]+$/.test(hash)) {
        targetComment = hash.substring(1);

      // Configure commenting API:
      var configJso = {

      var provider = {

      };

      var render = function() {
        if (window.goog &amp;&amp; window.goog.comments) {
          var holder = document.getElementById('comment-holder');
          window.goog.comments.render(holder, provider);
        }
      };

      // render now, or queue to render when library loads:
      if (window.goog &amp;&amp; window.goog.comments) {
        render();
      } else {
        window.goog = window.goog || {};
        window.goog.comments = window.goog.comments || {};
        window.goog.comments.loadQueue = window.goog.comments.loadQueue || [];
        window.goog.comments.loadQueue.push(render);
      }
    })();
// ]]&gt;
                     </script>
                     <div id="comment-holder">

                            <p class="comment-content" id="bc_0_76MC">
                             Hi! Great pattern!  It's so fun and different.  I'm a new crocheter and I'm not the best at reading patterns.  I suggest to anybody else new at crocheting who may be attempting this pattern to have the regular Granny Square mastered first.  I tried to make the owl square before I learned the granny square and it kept coming out round.  After I made the granny square and figured out how to math-it-out the owl square became square in my next attempt.
                             <br/>
                             <br/>
                             Thanks again for sharing, they're truly wonderful!
                             <br/>
                             <br/>
                             -Becca

                           <div class="comment-block" id="c6340589442020722986">
                            <div class="comment-header" id="bc_0_109M" kind="m">
                             <cite class="user">
                              <a href="https://www.blogger.com/profile/12784448725348924193" rel="nofollow">
                               Ali
                              </a>
                             </cite>
                             <span class="icon user">
                             </span>
                             <span class="datetime secondary-text">
                              <a href="http://www.repeatcrafterme.com/2012/11/owl-granny-square-crochet-pattern.html?showComment=1414249331117#c6340589442020722986" rel="nofollow">
                               October 25, 2014 at 8:02 AM
                              </a>
                             </span>
                            </div>
                            <p class="comment-content" id="bc_0_109MC">
                             HDC, in next stitch: DC - TC - DC, SC in next 5, in next stitch: DC - TC - DC, HDC in next, slip stitch to join - I did mine and realise the top as all ruffled as I'd read the pattern as being 5 stitches in the middle of DC-TC-DC-SC. When it should be first stitch is HDC-DC-TC-DC, then in the next 5 stitches do SC, then in 7th stitch do DC-TC-DC-HDC. Just in case anyone else read it wrong like me.
                             <br/>
                             <br/>
                             Also  I didn't understand how you wrote the first lot of double crochets in the 8 chain spaces. But I then figured out you do 2 lots of 3 double crochets for the corner with a chain space in between them,and then 3 double crochets in the next and then repeat that around 4 times. I am sure it's me unable to follow the pattern and not the pattern fault, only been crocheting since January. Love this pattern, will be making many more now I've worked out what I'm doing. Thanks for sharing it, love Kat's blog too, just making her crochet roses hearts.
                            </p>

                            <p class="comment-content" id="bc_0_128MC">
                             I started an Owl Granny Square afghan in May after the second time A friend sent me this link.   Today I got it for the third time so I decided to state my progress.  I decided on making 55 squares with 5 different color squares behind the Owls.  I also decided early on NOT to use buttons.  110 buttons just sounded too much.  So I'm making a 6 prong starburst in the center of each white circle.  Very Cute.
                             <br/>
                             To try and help out Nana/Addie I'll give you a bit of information on what I've used.   First I am using mostly leftover yarn  that was donated to our Senior Center.  I did have to purchase black yarn.Red Heart Super Saver from Walmart.  744 yds.   I do not know for sure if this will be enough for each square and for the borders.  For the Owl I used one skein of a very light pink, and two browns probably equal to one skein. I also had to use 2 different greens.  Remember I'm using leftovers here.  Since I was only doing 11 squares with each color scheme I only needed about a half of skein of each.   My 5 color schemes after the green row.  1. Medium blue and medium brown 2.light green and Burgundy, 3. Light purple and deep red  4. dark purple and Olive green and finally 5 Dark purple and rust.  All of these have one row of black around them.  I know the color scheme sounds strange but since I wasn't going to make all the squares exact I decided to just go for whatever I could find in the donation closet.  Addie I'll post pictures on my blog for the next couple of weeks    terryhathaway@blogspot.com
                             <br/>
                            </p>
